Jori lingered by the projection frame, support brace folded under one arm. "It is weird."

"What is?"

"Green not meaning go."

"Yes."

"Good weird."

"Yes."

He looked at the dark indicator. "Do you think people will remember?"

"No."

He frowned.

"Not always," Lena said. "That is why we make them practice."

"Like valve drills."

"Like valve drills."

He seemed satisfied, which at his age meant he immediately found a new problem. "The simulator label says training only. It should say training can still be wrong."

Lena looked at the label.

"You are correct."

"I know."

"Do not get used to it."

He smiled, quick and tired and young. Then Tamsa called from the corridor, "Apprentice Pell, if you are still bothering geometry, I am making you inventory gasket sizes."

Jori raised his voice. "She admitted I was correct."

"Then inventory correctly."

He groaned and went.

Lena watched him disappear into the corridor. He walked better now. Not well. Better. That was most of Kestrel.

Maro came in as Jori left, carrying a sealed packet. "External preservation copy for your old inquiry correction."

Lena took it but did not open it. "Final?"

"Nothing is final. It is binding enough to hurt the right archives."

"Good."

"Your adverse finding is formally vacated pending full doctrine review."

She looked at the packet.

For years, she had imagined that sentence as a door. Open it and something would return: the person before disgrace, the certainty before war, the clean anger before evidence complicated it. Now the packet felt important and insufficient in her hand.

"Thank you," she said.

Maro nodded. "Your correction is linked to the public record, not separated as personal relief."

"Also good."

"It means some people will keep using your name."

"They already were."

"Yes."

"At least now the record can argue back."

He accepted that. "Ilya is submitting another Ceyr archive tonight. Keva's physical copy has been fully mirrored. Sol's office is contesting preservation. Vale has gone quiet again."

"Quiet is not gone."

"No."

They stood beside the dark simulator.

Maro said, "Do you ever wish this had ended with an arrest?"

"Sometimes."

"A confession?"

"We had several."

"A cleaner one."

Lena looked toward the corridor where the schedule wall glowed beyond the bay. "Clean endings are dangerous around dirty systems."

Maro's mouth moved slightly. "Put that in findings?"

"Please don't."

He almost smiled and left with the unsteady gait of someone learning rest by enforcement.

Lena opened the packet after he was gone.

The correction was exactly as stiff as she expected. Compact Route Authority acknowledged material procedural defects, withheld evidence context, and improper reliance on narrowed doctrine during her war inquiry. It vacated the adverse finding. It restored standing subject to current medical clearance and charter role. It did not say sorry. Pellon had attached a note:

This does not repair the years. It changes what the years are allowed to prove.

That was better than sorry.

Lena sealed the packet and carried it to the quiet ledger room.

She did not file it among the dead. That would have been obscene. She filed a copy under institutional corrections, beside Keva's confession, Sivek's pressure disclosure, Ilya's Ceyr statements, Maro's privacy ruling, and the Ardent bulletin. The room was not only for deaths now. It had become a place where Kestrel stored truths too heavy for a schedule wall.

Eda Malk's note remained near the entrance.

She sang badly on purpose when people were scared.

Lena stood before it and wondered what song belonged to a station that had learned to mistrust green. Probably something ugly. Probably seventeen verses. Probably maintenance.

When she returned to Control, the night shift was taking over.

Sivek was leaving for a mandatory rest cycle with the expression of a man being escorted from his own guilt. Tamsa was arguing with Aven over whether Halcyon pump drills could be made less disruptive without making them less real. Vela was teaching Ari how to read deletion logs and pretending not to enjoy teaching. Om was asleep in a chair with a pencil still in hand; no one dared move her. Sann was on Morrow watch. Oret's Halcyon feed showed Dock North-Four busy, open, and undecorated. Jori and Niko had taped a new label under the simulator camera:

TRAINING CAN STILL BE WRONG.

This time, nobody removed it.

Lena took her place at geometry.

The route model loaded slowly. Kestrel-Halcyon Working Route. Restricted capacity. No general transit. Drone Two draft pending. Cancellation conditions active. Public witness assigned. Memorial links intact. Evidence mirrors stable. Life-support first.

The old gate would have been easier to love.

The new route was harder to betray.

Lena set the inquiry correction packet beside her console, not as proof that she was clean, but as evidence that records could change when enough people refused to let them sit still.

Outside, Vane Three carried names.

Halcyon breathed through new membranes.

Blue Vault stayed sealed.

Somewhere beyond the debris lanes, Cassian Vale remained a problem with a source clock. Somewhere inside the Compact, Eren Sol's sentences were being taken apart by people who had once admired them. Somewhere in cargo routes not yet touched by Kestrel, Min-7 sensors were being retested under lights that did not flatter them.

The work had escaped the station.

That was frightening.

That was the point.

The green simulator light blinked once as the next drill initialized.

Ari read the line from the board, voice steadier than before. "Condition pending."

Lena put her hands near the controls, not on them.

"Geometry watching," she said.

No one said go.

Not yet.

This time, that meant they were learning.
